style="text-align: left;">\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2006_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="Timeline of the 2006 Pacific hurricane season">Timeline of the 2006 Pacific hurricane season</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/2006_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2006 Atlantic hurricane season">2006 Atlantic hurricane season</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/2006_Pacific_typhoon_season" Ocean cyclone season</a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td class="hlist noprint nowrap" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; padding-top: 3px;"><a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">Pacific hurricane seasons</a><br/>\n<a href="/wiki/2004_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2004 Pacific hurricane season">2004</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2005 Pacific hurricane season">2005</a>, <b>2006</b>, <a href="/wiki/2007_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2007 Pacific hurricane season">2007</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2008 Pacific hurricane season">2008</a></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The <b>2006 Pacific hurricane season</b> was the most active since <a href="/wiki/2000_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2000 Pacific hurricane season">2000</a>, producing 19\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical storms</a> or hurricanes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epachurdat_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-epachurdat-1">[1]</a></sup> Eighteen developed within the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> (NHC) area of warning responsibility, which is east of <a href="/wiki/140th_meridian_west" title="140th meridian west">140\xc2\xb0W</a>, and one storm formed between <a href="/wiki/140th_meridian_west" title="140th meridian west">140\xc2\xb0W</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a>, which is under the jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">Central Pacific Hurricane Center</a> (CPHC). Of the 19\xc2\xa0total storms, eleven became hurricanes, of which six attained <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales" title="Tropical cyclone scales">major hurricane status</a>. Within the NHC portion of the basin, the season officially began on May 15, and in the CPHC portion, it started on June 1; the season officially ended on November 30. These dates conventionally delimit the period of each year when most tropical cyclones form in the eastern <a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">Pacific basin</a>.</p>\n<p>The strongest storm of the season was <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ioke" title="Hurricane Ioke">Hurricane Ioke</a>, which reached <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Pacific_hurricanes" title="List of Category 5 Pacific hurricanes">Category 5</a> status on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson scale</a> in the central Pacific Ocean; Ioke passed near <a href="/wiki/Johnston_Atoll" title="Johnston Atoll">Johnston Atoll</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a>, where it caused heavy damage but no deaths. The deadliest storm of the season was <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_John_(2006)" title="Hurricane John (2006)">Hurricane John</a>, which killed six people after striking the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a>, and the costliest storm was <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lane_(2006)" title="Hurricane Lane (2006)">Hurricane Lane</a>, which caused $203\xc2\xa0million in damage in southwestern Mexico (2006\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a>, $241\xc2\xa0million 2017\xc2\xa0USD).</p>\n<p>Seasonal activity began on May 27, when <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Aletta_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Aletta (2006)">Tropical Storm Aletta</a> formed off the southwest coast of Mexico. No storms formed in June, though the season became active in July when five named storms developed, including <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Daniel_(2006)" title="Hurricane Daniel (2006)">Hurricane Daniel</a> which was the second strongest storm of the season, as well as <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Emilia_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Emilia (2006)">Tropical Storm Emilia</a>. During August, Hurricanes Ioke and John formed, as well as four other storms. September was a relatively quiet month with two storms, of which one was Hurricane Lane. Three storms developed in October including <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Paul_(2006)" title="Hurricane Paul (2006)">Hurricane Paul</a> and two formed in November; this marked the second time on record, after <a href="/wiki/1961_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1961 Pacific hurricane season">1961</a>, when more than one tropical storm developed in the basin during the month of November.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Seasonal_forecast"><span margin-left:1em; text-align:right;">\n<caption><b>Predictions of tropical activity in the 2006 season<br/>\nfor the Eastern North Pacific</b></caption>\n<tr style="background:#ccf;">\n<td style="text-align:center;"><b>Source</b></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><b>Date</b></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><b><span style="font-size: 80%;">Named<br/>\nstorms</span></b></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><b><span style="font-size: 80%;">Hurricanes</span></b></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><b><span style="font-size: 80%;">Major<br/>\nhurricanes</span></b></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="left"><a href="/wiki/Climate_Prediction_Center" title="Climate Prediction Center">CPC</a></td>\n<td align="left"><i>Average</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noaa-EPac_avg_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-noaa-EPac_avg-2">[2]</a></sup></td>\n<td>15.3</td>\n<td>8.8</td>\n<td>4.2</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="left">NOAA</td>\n<td align="left">May 22, 2006</td>\n<td>12\xe2\x80\x9316</td>\n<td>6\xe2\x80\x938</td>\n<td>1\xe2\x80\x933</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="left"></td>\n<td align="left"><b>Actual activity</b></td>\n<td>18</td>\n<td>10</td>\n<td>5</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On May 22, 2006, the <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a>\'s (NOAA) <a href="/wiki/Climate_Prediction_Center" title="Climate Prediction Center">CPC</a> (CPC) released their forecasts for the 2006 <a href="/wiki/2006_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2006 Atlantic hurricane season">Atlantic</a> and Pacific hurricane seasons. The Pacific season was expected to be hindered by the decades-long cycle that began in <a href="/wiki/1995_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1995 Pacific hurricane season">1995</a>, which generally increased <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> across the basin. NOAA predicted a below-normal level of activity in the Eastern Pacific, with 12\xe2\x80\x9316\xc2\xa0named storms, of which 6\xe2\x80\x938 were expected to become hurricanes, and 1\xe2\x80\x933 expected to become major hurricanes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_May_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_May-3">[3]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">Central Pacific Hurricane Center</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Area_of_responsibility" title="Area of responsibility">area of responsibility</a> was also expected to be below average, with only two to three tropical cyclones expected to form or cross into the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_May_CP_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_May_CP-4">[4]</a></sup> They expected that neither <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o_Southern_Oscillation" title="El Ni\xc3\xb1o Southern Oscillation">El Ni\xc3\xb1o</a> nor La Ni\xc3\xb1a would affect conditions significantly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_May_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_May-3">[3]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On May 15, the hurricane season began in the Eastern Pacific basin, which is the area of the northern <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> east of 140\xc2\xb0<a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">W</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> On June 1, the season began in the Central Pacific warning zone (between 140\xc2\xb0<a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">W</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Dateline" title="International Dateline">International Dateline</a>); however, no storms occurred in the region until July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasonal_summary">Seasonal summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Seasonal summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2006_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="Timeline of the 2006 Pacific hurricane season">Timeline of the 2006 Pacific hurricane season</a></div>\n<center>\n<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map id="timeline_a8c4a7ec999ba84e900d57a2c6c05ce5" name="timeline_a8c4a7ec999ba84e900d57a2c6c05ce5">\n<area alt="Hurricane Paul (2006)" coords="641,57,727,77" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Paul_(2006)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Paul (2006)"/>\n<area alt="Hurricane Lane (2006)" coords="502,69,588,90" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lane_(2006)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Lane (2006)"/>\n<area alt="Hurricane John (2006)" coords="452,44,539,65" href="/wiki/Hurricane_John_(2006)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane John (2006)"/>\n<area alt="Hurricane Ioke" coords="424,20,510,41" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ioke" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Ioke"/>\n<area alt="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale" coords="602,170,804,190" href="/wiki/Saffir%2DSimpson_Hurricane_Scale" shape="rect" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale"/></map><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/a8c4a7ec999ba84e900d57a2c6c05ce5.png" usemap="#timeline_a8c4a7ec999ba84e900d57a2c6c05ce5"/></div>\n</center>\n<p>No tropical storms developed in June in the basin, which was unusual compared to the average of two storms forming during the month. Since 1966, there have been only three other seasons in which a tropical storm did not form in June, these being <a href="/wiki/1969_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1969 Pacific hurricane season">1969</a>, <a href="/wiki/2004_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2004 Pacific hurricane season">2004</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2007_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2007 Pacific hurricane season">2007</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> After such an inactive month, the tropics became active in July when five named storms developed, including <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Daniel_(2006)" title="Hurricane Daniel (2006)">Hurricane Daniel</a> which was the second strongest storm of the season. During August, Hurricanes Ioke and John formed, as well as four other storms. September was a relatively quiet month with two storms, of which one was Hurricane Lane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup> By that time, however, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o-Southern_Oscillation" title="El Ni\xc3\xb1o-Southern Oscillation">El Ni\xc3\xb1o</a> conditions became established across the Pacific,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup> which is known to enhance <a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">Pacific hurricane</a> activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_May_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_May-3">[3]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Three storms developed in October, including Hurricane Paul. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup> Tropical activity within the basin in November\xc2\xa02006 was the most active on record, based on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accumulated_Cyclone_Energy" title="Accumulated Cyclone Energy">Accumulated Cyclone Energy</a> (ACE) Index. Three tropical cyclones formed, of which two became tropical storms; only two other seasons on record, <a href="/wiki/1961_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1961 Pacific hurricane season">1961</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2015 Pacific hurricane season">2015</a>, produced two tropical storms in the month of November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nov06_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-nov06-10">[10]</a></sup> In addition, Mexico was struck by four tropical cyclones in 2006, none on the Atlantic coast and all along the Pacific coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmo_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-wmo-11">[11]</a></sup> One hit <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a> while the others made landfall on the mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_Book_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_Book-12">[12]</a></sup></p>\n<p>An <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical</a> storm persisted in the extreme northern central Pacific Ocean in late October. It drifted over unusually <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">warm waters</a> up to 3.6\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (2\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) above normal, and gradually developed convection near the center. By November 2, <a href="/wiki/QuikSCAT" title="QuikSCAT">QuikSCAT</a> satellite suggested the system attained winds of up to 60\xc2\xa0mph (95\xc2\xa0km/h) about 900\xc2\xa0mi (1450\xc2\xa0km) west of <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>. The system also developed an <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> and an eyewall. The cyclone tracked northeastward as it gradually weakened, and dissipated on November 4. <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> considered the cyclone to be a <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_cyclone" title="Subtropical cyclone">subtropical storm</a>. However, as it formed outside of the territory of any monitoring organization, it was not named. Operationally, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> treated the system as a tropical disturbance, numbered 91C.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-91C_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-91C-13">[13]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Aletta">Tropical Storm Aletta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Aletta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Storm_Aletta_(2006).jpg"><img alt="Tropical Storm Aletta (2006).jpg" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="4000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Tropical_Storm_Aletta_%282006%29.jpg/150px-Tropical_Storm_Aletta_%282006%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Tropical_Storm_Aletta_%282006%29.jpg/225px-Tropical_Storm_Aletta_%282006%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Tropical_Storm_Aletta_%282006%29.jpg/300px-Tropical_Storm_Aletta_%282006%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aletta_2006_track.png"><img alt="Aletta 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Aletta_2006_track.png/300px-Aletta_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>May 27\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 May 30</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>45\xc2\xa0mph (75\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1002\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Aletta_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Aletta (2006)">Tropical Storm Aletta (2006)</a></div>\n<p>On May\xc2\xa027, 12\xc2\xa0days into the season, Tropical Depression One formed about 190\xc2\xa0miles (305\xc2\xa0km) south of Acapulco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atcr_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-atcr-14">[14]</a></sup> It slowly organized and became a tropical storm with 45\xc2\xa0mph (75\xc2\xa0km/h) sustained winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atcr_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-atcr-14">[14]</a></sup> While named tropical cyclones in May are infrequent events, Aletta marked the seventh consecutive year to have a named cyclone form in May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHC_May_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHC_May-15">[15]</a></sup> The storm moved toward the <a href="/wiki/Guerrero" title="Guerrero">Guerrero</a> coast in southwestern Mexico, prompting the Mexican government to issue <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm_watch" title="Tropical storm watch">tropical storm watches</a> between <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Punta_Maldonado&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Punta Maldonado (page does not exist)">Punta Maldonado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zihuatanejo" title="Zihuatanejo">Zihuatanejo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMN_Aletta_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-SMN_Aletta-16">[16]</a></sup> Aletta then became stationary over the <a href="/wiki/Guerrero" title="Guerrero">Guerrero</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oaxaca" title="Oaxaca">Oaxaca</a> coastlines, but it later turned to the west and dissipated on May\xc2\xa030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atcr_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-atcr-14">[14]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Aletta produced moderate rainfall across Mexico, including a 24-hour rainfall total of 3.94\xc2\xa0inches (100\xc2\xa0mm)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[nb 1]</a></sup> in Jacatepec, Oaxaca on May\xc2\xa030, and 3.78\xc2\xa0inches (96\xc2\xa0mm) in La Calera, Guerrero, the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMN_Aletta_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-SMN_Aletta-16">[16]</a></sup> There were no reports of damage, flooding, or casualties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atcr_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-atcr-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHC_May_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-NHC_May-15">[15]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Two-E">Tropical Depression Two-E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Two-E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Depression_Two-E_(2006).PNG"><img alt="Tropical Depression Two-E (2006).PNG" data-file-height="652" data-file-width="730" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Tropical_Depression_Two-E_%282006%29.PNG/150px-Tropical_Depression_Two-E_%282006%29.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Tropical_Depression_Two-E_%282006%29.PNG/225px-Tropical_Depression_Two-E_%282006%29.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Tropical_Depression_Two-E_%282006%29.PNG/300px-Tropical_Depression_Two-E_%282006%29.PNG 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Two-E_2006_track.png"><img alt="Two-E 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Two-E_2006_track.png/150px-Two-E_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Two-E_2006_track.png/225px-Two-E_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Two-E_2006_track.png/300px-Two-E_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>June 3\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 June 5</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>35\xc2\xa0mph (55\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1005\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Depression_Two-E_(2006)" title="Tropical Depression Two-E (2006)">Tropical Depression Two-E (2006)</a></div>\n<p>On the day after Aletta dissipated, a new area of disturbed weather developed off the southwest Mexican coast. High shear slowed the development of the system, although it gained enough convection and organization to be classified as a tropical depression on June\xc2\xa03. The depression strengthened to near tropical storm status as it approached the coast of southwestern Mexico; however, shear persisted over the system and it weakened before dissipating on June\xc2\xa04.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2tcr_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-2tcr-18">[17]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Despite never becoming a named storm, heavy rain occurred, including a total of 19.13\xc2\xa0inches (486\xc2\xa0mm) measured in a 48\xe2\x80\x91hour period in Acapulco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> Mudslides and flash flooding were reported,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2tcr_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-2tcr-18">[17]</a></sup> forcing 72\xc2\xa0people from their homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> No deaths or serious damage was reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2tcr_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-2tcr-18">[17]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Bud">Hurricane Bud</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Hurricane Bud">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bud_(2006)" title="Hurricane Bud (2006)">Hurricane Bud (2006)</a></div>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3\xc2\xa0hurricane\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane bud 2006.jpg" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="4000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg/150px-Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg/225px-Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg/300px-Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bud_2006_track.png"><img alt="Bud 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Bud_2006_track.png/150px-Bud_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Bud_2006_track.png/225px-Bud_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Bud_2006_track.png/300px-Bud_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 11\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 July 16</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>125\xc2\xa0mph (205\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 953\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On July\xc2\xa011, after over a month of inactivity, a disturbance off the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Peninsula of Baja California</a> developed into a tropical depression. It moved west-northwestward for its entire duration, quickly intensifying into a tropical storm and hurricane. A clear, well-defined <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> developed, and Bud became the first <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales" title="Tropical cyclone scales">major hurricane</a> of the season. On July\xc2\xa013, the hurricane attained peak winds of 125\xc2\xa0mph (205\xc2\xa0km/h), although cooler waters and stable air caused a marked weakening trend. By July\xc2\xa015, Bud weakened to tropical depression status, and the next day it degenerated into a remnant low pressure area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> The remnants of Bud produced light rainfall across <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jul06_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-jul06-22">[21]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Carlotta">Hurricane Carlotta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Hurricane Carlotta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1\xc2\xa0hurricane\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane carlotta 2006.jpg" data-file-height="5400" data-file-width="5400" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg/150px-Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg/225px-Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg/300px-Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carlotta_2006_track.png"><img alt="Carlotta 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Carlotta_2006_track.png/150px-Carlotta_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Carlotta_2006_track.png/225px-Carlotta_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Carlotta_2006_track.png/300px-Carlotta_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 12\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 July 16</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>85\xc2\xa0mph (140\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 981\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>A tropical wave exited Africa on June\xc2\xa030 and moved across the Atlantic Ocean without development. On July\xc2\xa09, while crossing Central America into the eastern North Pacific Ocean, thunderstorm activity increased, and the system organized into Tropical Depression Four-E early on July\xc2\xa012 about 290\xc2\xa0mi (465\xc2\xa0km) south of <a href="/wiki/Zihuatanejo" title="Zihuatanejo">Zihuatanejo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guerrero" title="Guerrero">Guerrero</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup> The large depression moved quickly to the west-northwest to the south of a <a href="/wiki/Ridge_(meteorology)" title="Ridge (meteorology)">ridge</a> over northwestern Mexico, and its outer rainbands moved across the coast. Rainfall totals were less than 1\xc2\xa0inch (25\xc2\xa0mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup> The depression intensified into Tropical Storm Carlotta just six hours after forming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup> By late on July\xc2\xa012, the storm developed <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone#Physical_structure" title="Tropical cyclone">banding features</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> and early on July\xc2\xa013 Carlotta attained hurricane status about 430\xc2\xa0mi (700\xc2\xa0km) south of the southern tip of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baja_California_peninsula" title="Baja California peninsula">Baja California peninsula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup></p>\n<p>As Carlotta intensified, the system became more compact, and it reached peak winds of 85\xc2\xa0mph (140\xc2\xa0km/h) on July\xc2\xa013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> formed in the center, and the hurricane was briefly forecast to attain <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales" title="Tropical cyclone scales">major hurricane</a> status, or a Category\xc2\xa03 on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson scale</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> However, Carlotta weakened due to increased wind shear from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bud_(2006)" title="Hurricane Bud (2006)">Hurricane Bud</a> to its west,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup> and the eye and convection deteriorated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> Carlotta briefly weakened to tropical storm status late on July\xc2\xa014, although a decrease in shear allowed it to reintensify into a hurricane. This was short-lived as the center moved into the area of cooler waters, and Carlotta again weakened to tropical storm status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-6"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup> Late on July\xc2\xa015, the circulation became separated from the convection,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> and Carlotta weakened to tropical depression status on July\xc2\xa016, and the next day generated into a remnant low. The circulation continued generally westward, dissipating on July\xc2\xa020 about 1500\xc2\xa0mi (2400\xc2\xa0km) east of the Hawaiian islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-7"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Daniel">Hurricane Daniel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Hurricane Daniel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4\xc2\xa0hurricane\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane daniel 2006.jpg" data-file-height="4320" data-file-width="4320" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg/150px-Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg/225px-Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg/300px-Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Daniel_2006_track.png"><img alt="Daniel 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Daniel_2006_track.png/150px-Daniel_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Daniel_2006_track.png/225px-Daniel_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Daniel_2006_track.png/300px-Daniel_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 16\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 July 26</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>150\xc2\xa0mph (240\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 933\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Daniel_(2006)" title="Hurricane Daniel (2006)">Hurricane Daniel (2006)</a></div>\n<p>On July\xc2\xa016, a tropical disturbance formed far to the south of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a> and quickly increased in convective activity and organization, becoming a tropical depression. The system continued to organize and was designated as a tropical storm the next day. On July\xc2\xa018, Daniel attained hurricane status, and two days later underwent rapid intensification; it reached <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales" title="Tropical cyclone scales">major hurricane status</a> and was later upgraded further to Category\xc2\xa04 status on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale</a>. Its peak intensity was 150\xc2\xa0mph (240\xc2\xa0km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-danieltcr_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-danieltcr-28">[27]</a></sup> The hurricane underwent <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eyewall replacement cycles</a>, which are internal mechanisms that occur in most intense hurricanes. Daniel later became an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annular_hurricane" title="Annular hurricane">annular hurricane</a>, which allowed it to maintain Category\xc2\xa04 status for longer than it otherwise would have.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-danialdisc16_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-danialdisc16-29">[28]</a></sup></p>\n<p>It crossed over into the Central Pacific early on July\xc2\xa024 and was predicted to affect Hawaii as a tropical storm; however, Daniel encountered weak steering currents in the open ocean, causing it to slow down considerably.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-danieltcr_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-danieltcr-28">[27]</a></sup> It rapidly degenerated to a tropical depression on July\xc2\xa025, and the CPHC issued its last advisory on July\xc2\xa026 while the storm was still well to the east of Hawaii. Its remnants later moved across the Hawaiian islands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-danieltcr_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-danieltcr-28">[27]</a></sup> dropping heavy rainfall and causing flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup> West Wailuaiki on Maui recorded 3.87\xc2\xa0inches (98\xc2\xa0mm) in one day, which was the highest daily rainfall total from the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jul06_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-jul06-22">[21]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Emilia">Tropical Storm Emilia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Emilia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_Emilia_2006.jpg"><img alt="TS Emilia 2006.jpg" data-file-height="4800" data-file-width="4800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/TS_Emilia_2006.jpg/150px-TS_Emilia_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/TS_Emilia_2006.jpg/225px-TS_Emilia_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/TS_Emilia_2006.jpg/300px-TS_Emilia_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emilia_2006_track.png"><img alt="Emilia 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Emilia_2006_track.png/150px-Emilia_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Emilia_2006_track.png/225px-Emilia_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Emilia_2006_track.png/300px-Emilia_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 21\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 July 28</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>65\xc2\xa0mph (100\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 990\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Emilia_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Emilia (2006)">Tropical Storm Emilia (2006)</a></div>\n<p>The origins of Emilia were from a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> that developed into a tropical depression on July\xc2\xa021, a short distance off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a>. It moved generally north-northwestward, reaching tropical storm status on July\xc2\xa022 and passing about 175\xc2\xa0mi (280\xc2\xa0km) southwest of <a href="/wiki/Manzanillo,_Colima" title="Manzanillo, Colima">Manzanillo, Colima</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etcr_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-etcr-30">[29]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eyewall</a> began to form that day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> and Emilia reached peak winds of 65\xc2\xa0mph (105\xc2\xa0km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etcr_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-etcr-30">[29]</a></sup> It briefly weakened due to <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, although restrengthening occurred as the storm turned toward the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baja_California_peninsula" title="Baja California peninsula">Baja California peninsula</a>. On July\xc2\xa026, Emilia again reached peak winds of 65\xc2\xa0mph (105\xc2\xa0km/h), and shortly thereafter it passed about 60\xc2\xa0mi (95\xc2\xa0km) southwest of the southern tip of Baja California. It weakened as it turned into cooler waters, first to tropical depression status on July\xc2\xa027 and then to a convective-less remnant low on July\xc2\xa028. The remnants dissipated on July\xc2\xa031 about 495\xc2\xa0mi (800\xc2\xa0km) west-southwest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego,_California" title="San Diego, California">San Diego, California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etcr_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-etcr-30">[29]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In southwestern Mexico, Emilia produced tropical storm force winds along the coastline. Rainfall in the southern portion of the Baja California peninsula caused minor flooding, and gusty winds caused damage to buildings and power lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etcr_30-3"><a href="#cite_note-etcr-30">[29]</a></sup> Moisture from Emilia reached the southwestern United States. Thunderstorms and rainfall occurred across Arizona, causing flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> In southern California, the storm dropped light rainfall, which assisted firefighters in containing a wildfire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Fabio">Tropical Storm Fabio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Fabio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg"><img alt="Tropical Storm Fabio 2006.jpg" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="700" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg/150px-Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg/225px-Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg/300px-Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fabio_2006_track.png"><img alt="Fabio 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Fabio_2006_track.png/150px-Fabio_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Fabio_2006_track.png/225px-Fabio_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Fabio_2006_track.png/300px-Fabio_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 31\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 August 3</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>50\xc2\xa0mph (85\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1000\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>A tropical wave crossed the west coast of Africa on July\xc2\xa015 and entered the Pacific on July\xc2\xa025. Convection increased on July\xc2\xa028, and at 1800\xc2\xa0UTC on July\xc2\xa031 the system became Tropical Depression Seven-E about 980\xc2\xa0miles (1,580\xc2\xa0km) southwest of the southern tip of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baja_California_peninsula" title="Baja California peninsula">Baja California peninsula</a>. Six hours later, the depression was upgraded to Tropical Storm Fabio. It moved westward due to a ridge to its north, and on August\xc2\xa01 Fabio reached peak winds of 50\xc2\xa0mph (85\xc2\xa0km/h). Later, the storm began weakening due to increased <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> and dry air. On August\xc2\xa03, Fabio deteriorated to tropical depression status, and later that day it degenerated into a remnant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">low pressure area</a>. The remnants continued westward, moving across <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> on August\xc2\xa07.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ftcr_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-ftcr-34">[33]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Although Fabio did not impact land, its remnants produced heavy rainfall in Hawaii. In a 24-hour period, 2.89\xc2\xa0inches (73\xc2\xa0mm) of rainfall was recorded at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Glenwood,_Hawaii&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Glenwood, Hawaii (page does not exist)">Glenwood</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_(island)" title="Hawaii (island)">Hawaii</a>; this was the highest daily rainfall total for the month on the island. However, the heaviest precipitation fell on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Wai%CA%BBale%CA%BBale" title="Mount Wai\xca\xbbale\xca\xbbale">Mount Wai\xca\xbbale\xca\xbbale</a> on <a href="/wiki/Kauai" title="Kauai">Kauai</a>, where 15.08\xc2\xa0inches (383\xc2\xa0mm) fell in 24\xc2\xa0hours; this total alone was greater than all other monthly rainfall totals in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hawrain_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-hawrain-35">[34]</a></sup> The heavy rainfall flooded the <a href="/wiki/Hanalei_River" title="Hanalei River">Hanalei River</a>, which forced the closure of the Kuhio Highway when a bridge was inundated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ftcr_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-ftcr-34">[33]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Oahu" title="Oahu">Oahu</a>, the rainfall caused ponding on roadways and flooding along streams. One flooded stream stranded 24\xc2\xa0hikers along a trail, all of whom required rescue by helicopter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Gilma">Tropical Storm Gilma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Gilma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg"><img alt="TS Gilma 2006BW.jpg" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg/150px-TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg/225px-TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg/300px-TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gilma_2006_track.png"><img alt="Gilma 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Gilma_2006_track.png/150px-Gilma_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Gilma_2006_track.png/225px-Gilma_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Gilma_2006_track.png/300px-Gilma_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 1\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 August 3</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>40\xc2\xa0mph (65\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1004\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On July\xc2\xa017, a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> exited Africa and crossed the Atlantic without developing. On July\xc2\xa025 it entered the Eastern Pacific, gradually developing an area of organized convection. Despite marginally favorable upper-level winds, the system organized enough to be declared a tropical depression on August\xc2\xa01, several hundred miles southwest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acapulco,_Mexico" title="Acapulco, Mexico">Acapulco, Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gTCR_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-gTCR-37">[36]</a></sup> Initially, the depression tracked west-northwestward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup> Despite wind shear in the area,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> the depression was upgraded to Tropical Storm Gilma later on August\xc2\xa01. The wind shear prevented further strengthening or organization, and Gilma weakened to a tropical depression early on August\xc2\xa02.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gTCR_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-gTCR-37">[36]</a></sup> The depression turned westward,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup> and Gilma degenerated into a remnant low by August\xc2\xa04.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gTCR_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-gTCR-37">[36]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Hector">Hurricane Hector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Hurricane Hector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2\xc2\xa0hurricane\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane hector 2006.jpg" data-file-height="5200" data-file-width="5200" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg/150px-Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg/225px-Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg/300px-Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hector_2006_track.png"><img alt="Hector 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Hector_2006_track.png/150px-Hector_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Hector_2006_track.png/225px-Hector_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Hector_2006_track.png/300px-Hector_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 15\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 August 23</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>110\xc2\xa0mph (175\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 966\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>A tropical wave exited Africa on July\xc2\xa031, and after no development in the Atlantic, it crossed Central America into the northeastern Pacific Ocean on August\xc2\xa010. Convection gradually increased, and a broad <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">low pressure area</a> developed about 375\xc2\xa0miles (605\xc2\xa0km) south of <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco, Mexico</a> on August\xc2\xa013. The system continued to become organized, and it developed into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone#Tropical_Depression" title="Tropical Cyclone">tropical depression</a> around 1800\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on August\xc2\xa015 about 650\xc2\xa0mi (1,045\xc2\xa0km) south-southwest of the southern tip of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a>. It moved west-northwestward, located south of a <a href="/wiki/Ridge_(meteorology)" title="Ridge (meteorology)">ridge</a> that extended westward from northern Mexico westward into the Pacific. The depression quickly intensified into Tropical Storm Hector early on August\xc2\xa016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hectortcr_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hectortcr-39">[38]</a></sup> Hector was able to steadily strengthen, reaching hurricane status at 0600\xc2\xa0UTC on August\xc2\xa017. It is estimated that Hector reached its peak intensity of 110\xc2\xa0mph (175\xc2\xa0km/h) at 0600\xc2\xa0UTC on August\xc2\xa018, while centered about 1,035\xc2\xa0mi (1,665\xc2\xa0km) southwest of the southern tip of Baja California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Hector remained a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale#Category_2" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 2 hurricane</a> for about 24\xc2\xa0hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_8-5"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup> Shortly thereafter, it encountered cooler waters and westerly shear,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> and Hector steadily weakened until becoming a tropical storm by August\xc2\xa020. Shortly thereafter, the storm reached a weakness in the <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_ridge" title="Subtropical ridge">subtropical ridge</a>, which caused it to move slowly to the northwest. By August\xc2\xa021, deep convection was confined to the northeast portion of the circulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> The shear was not strong enough to completely weaken the tropical cyclone and Hector remained a tropical storm with 50\xc2\xa0mph (85\xc2\xa0km/h) winds for about 24\xc2\xa0hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hectortcr_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hectortcr-39">[38]</a></sup> After the remaining shower and thunderstorm activity dissipated on August\xc2\xa022, the cyclone turned westward in response to the low-level easterly wind flow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> Hector weakened to a tropical depression at 0000\xc2\xa0UTC on August\xc2\xa023, and to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">remnant low</a> six\xc2\xa0hours later. The remnant circulation of Hector dissipated on August\xc2\xa024 about 750\xc2\xa0mi (1,210\xc2\xa0km) east of the <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands" title="Hawaiian Islands">Hawaiian Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Ioke">Hurricane Ioke</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hurricane Ioke">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5\xc2\xa0hurricane\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Ioke,_MODIS_image_on_August_24,_2006,_2155_UTC.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane Ioke, MODIS image on August 24, 2006, 2155 UTC.jpg" data-file-height="4400" data-file-width="4400" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Hurricane_Ioke%2C_MODIS_image_on_August_24%2C_2006%2C_2155_UTC.jpg/150px-Hurricane_Ioke%2C_MODIS_image_on_August_24%2C_2006%2C_2155_UTC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Hurricane_Ioke%2C_MODIS_image_on_August_24%2C_2006%2C_2155_UTC.jpg/225px-Hurricane_Ioke%2C_MODIS_image_on_August_24%2C_2006%2C_2155_UTC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Hurricane_Ioke%2C_MODIS_image_on_August_24%2C_2006%2C_2155_UTC.jpg/300px-Hurricane_Ioke%2C_MODIS_image_on_August_24%2C_2006%2C_2155_UTC.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ioke_2006_track.png"><img alt="Ioke 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1476" data-file-width="2000" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ioke_2006_track.png/150px-Ioke_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ioke_2006_track.png/225px-Ioke_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ioke_2006_track.png/300px-Ioke_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 20\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 August 27 <small>(<a href="/wiki/2006_Pacific_typhoon_season#Typhoon_Ioke" title="2006 Pacific typhoon season">Exited basin</a>)</small></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>160\xc2\xa0mph (260\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 915\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ioke" title="Hurricane Ioke">Hurricane Ioke</a></div>\n<p>The cyclone developed from the <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">Intertropical Convergence Zone</a> on August\xc2\xa020 far to the south of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>. Encountering warm waters, little <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, and well-defined <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a>, Ioke intensified from a tropical depression to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 4</a> status within 48\xc2\xa0hours. Late on August\xc2\xa022 it rapidly weakened to Category\xc2\xa02 status before crossing over <a href="/wiki/Johnston_Atoll" title="Johnston Atoll">Johnston Atoll</a>. Two days later favorable conditions again allowed for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapid strengthening</a>, and Ioke attained Category\xc2\xa05 status on August 25\xc2\xa0before crossing the International Date Line. At the time, its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barometric_pressure" title="Barometric pressure">barometric pressure</a> was estimated at 915\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>, thus becoming the strongest hurricane on record in the Central Pacific.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup> As it continued westward its intensity fluctuated, and on August\xc2\xa031 it passed near <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a> with winds of 155\xc2\xa0mph (249\xc2\xa0km/h). Ioke gradually weakened as it turned northwestward and northward, and by September\xc2\xa06 it had transitioned into an <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iokeatcr_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-iokeatcr-44">[43]</a></sup> By then, the cyclone had lasted 19\xc2\xa0days, reaching the equivalent of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Pacific_hurricanes" title="List of Category 5 Pacific hurricanes">Category 5</a> status on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale</a> three times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup> The remnants of Ioke accelerated northeastward and ultimately crossed into <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cattlenet_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-cattlenet-45">[44]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Ioke did not affect any permanently populated areas in the Central Pacific or Western Pacific basins as a hurricane or a typhoon. A crew of 12\xc2\xa0people stayed in a hurricane-proof bunker on <a href="/wiki/Johnston_Atoll" title="Johnston Atoll">Johnston Atoll</a> during the hurricane\'s passage; the crew estimated winds reached over 100\xc2\xa0mph (160\xc2\xa0km/h), which damaged trees on the island but did not impact the island\'s bird population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> The hurricane left moderate damage on <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a> totaling $88\xc2\xa0million (2006\xc2\xa0USD), which resulted from blown off roofs and damaged buildings, although the infrastructure of the island was left intact. All military personnel were evacuated from the island, the first full-scale evacuation of the island since Typhoon Sarah in <a href="/wiki/1967_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="1967 Pacific typhoon season">1967</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-829afpn_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-829afpn-47">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> Later, the extratropical remnants of Ioke produced a severe storm surge along the <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaskan</a> coastline, causing beach erosion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncdc-50">[49]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Ileana">Hurricane Ileana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Hurricane Ileana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3\xc2\xa0hurricane\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane Ileana 23 aug 2006 1750Z.jpg" data-file-height="5000" data-file-width="5000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg/150px-Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg/225px-Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg/300px-Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a
