srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Ileana_2006_track.png/225px-Ileana_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Ileana_2006_track.png/300px-Ileana_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 21\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 August 27</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>120\xc2\xa0mph (195\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 955\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ileana_(2006)" title="Hurricane Ileana (2006)">Hurricane Ileana (2006)</a></div>\n<p>The origins of Hurricane Ileana were from a tropical wave that moved off the coast of Africa on August\xc2\xa08. It entered the Eastern North Pacific on August\xc2\xa016 and developed into a tropical depression on August\xc2\xa021 near <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a>. The depression strengthened into Tropical Storm Ileana six hours after forming. Ileana continued to strengthen, becoming a hurricane in 24\xc2\xa0hours and a major hurricane a day after that. Ileana reached its peak intensity of 120\xc2\xa0mph (195\xc2\xa0km/h) before beginning a slow weakening phase on August\xc2\xa024 when it encountered cooler waters. Ileana weakened a tropical depression on the morning of August\xc2\xa027 and quickly degenerated into a remnant low, dissipating on August\xc2\xa029.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Illeanatcr_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Illeanatcr-51">[50]</a></sup> As Ileana was heading north along the Mexican coastline, slight rainfall was recorded along the coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ileana_Rain_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ileana_Rain-52">[51]</a></sup> There were also reports of hurricane-force winds on <a href="/wiki/Socorro_Island" title="Socorro Island">Socorro Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Illeanatcr_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Illeanatcr-51">[50]</a></sup> One fatality was reported when a man drowned in heavy surf near <a href="/wiki/Cabo_San_Lucas" title="Cabo San Lucas">Cabo San Lucas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IlleanaDeath_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-IlleanaDeath-53">[52]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_John">Hurricane John</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Hurricane John">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4\xc2\xa0hurricane\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane John Aug 31 2006.jpg" data-file-height="6000" data-file-width="6000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg/150px-Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg/225px-Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg/300px-Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_2006_track.png"><img alt="John 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/John_2006_track.png/150px-John_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/John_2006_track.png/225px-John_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/John_2006_track.png/300px-John_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 28\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 September 4</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>130\xc2\xa0mph (215\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 948\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_John_(2006)" title="Hurricane John (2006)">Hurricane John (2006)</a></div>\n<p>On August\xc2\xa028, a persistent area of low pressure southwest of <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a>, Mexico developed into a tropical depression. Later that day it strengthened into a tropical storm, and it reached hurricane strength 24\xc2\xa0hours later on August\xc2\xa029. John underwent rapid intensification and reached Category\xc2\xa03 intensity later that day and Category\xc2\xa04 on August\xc2\xa030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jtcr_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-jtcr-54">[53]</a></sup> Hours later, the hurricane underwent another eyewall replacement cycle,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-johndisc10_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-johndisc10-55">[54]</a></sup> and subsequently weakened to Category\xc2\xa03 status as it paralleled the Mexican coastline a short distance offshore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-johndisc11_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-johndisc11-56">[55]</a></sup> Potentially due to its eyewall replacement cycle or its interaction with land, Hurricane John weakened to a 105\xc2\xa0mph hurricane by late on August\xc2\xa031,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-john14_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-john14-57">[56]</a></sup> but restrengthened to a major hurricane shortly after. It made landfall near the southern tip of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baja_California_peninsula" title="Baja California peninsula">Baja California peninsula</a> as a Category\xc2\xa02 hurricane on September\xc2\xa01.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-john19_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-john19-58">[57]</a></sup> John continued northwestward along the eastern Baja California peninsula, weakening to tropical depression status by September\xc2\xa03 and dissipating on September\xc2\xa04 in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_California" title="Gulf of California">Gulf of California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jtcr_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-jtcr-54">[53]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Along the southwestern coast of Mexico, Hurricane John produced heavy surf, strong winds, and heavy rainfall, which flooded roads, caused mudslides, and downed trees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jtcr_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-jtcr-54">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> Along the Baja California Peninsula, the hurricane dropped heavy rainfall, with a 24-hour peak of 10.8\xc2\xa0inches (276\xc2\xa0mm) in Los Planes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> The heavy rainfall caused flooding, closed roads,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lapaz_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-lapaz-61">[60]</a></sup> and caused a dam to overflow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fourdeaths_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-fourdeaths-62">[61]</a></sup> The winds and rainfall destroyed thousands of flimsy houses across the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bajadamage_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-bajadamage-63">[62]</a></sup> Across Mexico, five people were killed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jtcr_54-3"><a href="#cite_note-jtcr-54">[53]</a></sup> and damage amounted to $663\xc2\xa0million (2006\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Mexican_peso" title="Mexican peso">MXN</a>, $60.8\xc2\xa0million 2006\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mexicodamagetotal_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-mexicodamagetotal-64">[63]</a></sup> Moisture from the remnants of John produced flooding across Texas, which closed a \xc2\xbd\xc2\xa0mile (800\xc2\xa0m) portion of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_10" title="Interstate 10">Interstate 10</a> in El Paso.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foxnews_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-65">[64]</a></sup> In southern New Mexico, the rainfall caused widespread street flooding and some minor damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> Tropical moisture from the storm also produced rainfall in <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, where eight separate mudslides occurred, trapping 19\xc2\xa0vehicles but causing no injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-califor_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-califor-67">[66]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Kristy">Hurricane Kristy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Hurricane Kristy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Kristy_(2006)" title="Hurricane Kristy (2006)">Hurricane Kristy (2006)</a></div>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1\xc2\xa0hurricane\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg"><img alt="12E Hurricane Kristy 2006.jpg" data-file-height="4643" data-file-width="4419" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg/150px-12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg/225px-12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg/300px-12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kristy_2006_track.png"><img alt="Kristy 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Kristy_2006_track.png/150px-Kristy_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Kristy_2006_track.png/225px-Kristy_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Kristy_2006_track.png/300px-Kristy_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 30\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 September 8</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>80\xc2\xa0mph (130\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 985\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On August\xc2\xa030, a tropical wave located about 525\xc2\xa0miles (850\xc2\xa0km) south-southwest of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a> became more organized and was designated as the twelfth tropical depression of the 2006\xc2\xa0season. It strengthened into Tropical Storm Kristy and became Hurricane Kristy the next day. It did not retain this status for long, partly due to its proximity to Hurricane John.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ktcr_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-ktcr-68">[67]</a></sup> There was a possibility of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fujiwhara_interaction" title="Fujiwhara interaction">Fujiwhara interaction</a> between both systems, causing Kristy to weaken or perhaps be absorbed into the circulation of John.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> This did not occur, however. Kristy weakened steadily after its peak intensity and looked to be close to dissipating, but on September\xc2\xa03 and again on September\xc2\xa05, convection flared up and it returned to tropical storm strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ktcr_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-ktcr-68">[67]</a></sup> After oscillating between storm and depression strength, the system degenerated into a remnant low on September\xc2\xa07, which dissipated on September\xc2\xa08 without affecting land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ktcr_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-ktcr-68">[67]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Lane">Hurricane Lane</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Hurricane Lane">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3\xc2\xa0hurricane\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane Lane 16 sept 2006 aqua.jpg" data-file-height="6700" data-file-width="5600" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg/150px-Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg/225px-Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg/300px-Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lane_2006_track.png"><img alt="Lane 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Lane_2006_track.png/150px-Lane_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Lane_2006_track.png/225px-Lane_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Lane_2006_track.png/300px-Lane_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 13\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 September 17</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>125\xc2\xa0mph (205\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 952\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lane_(2006)" title="Hurricane Lane (2006)">Hurricane Lane (2006)</a></div>\n<p>On September\xc2\xa013, a tropical disturbance located about 125\xc2\xa0miles (200\xc2\xa0km) west-southwest of <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a>, Mexico, gradually became better organized and was designated the thirteenth tropical depression of the 2006\xc2\xa0season. The depression intensified in a favorable environment, and was upgraded to Tropical Storm Lane later that night. As it moved parallel to the Mexican coast it continued to strengthen and became a hurricane on September\xc2\xa015, and a major hurricane early the next day. Hurricane Lane reached peak winds of 125\xc2\xa0mph (205\xc2\xa0km/h) before it made landfall on the coast of <a href="/wiki/Sinaloa" title="Sinaloa">Sinaloa</a> on September\xc2\xa016. It quickly weakened over land and dissipated on September\xc2\xa017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ltcr_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-ltcr-70">[69]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Tropical Storm Lane produced heavy rainfall and high seas along the west coast of Mexico, including <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a> where flood waters reached 16\xc2\xa0inches (40\xc2\xa0cm) in depth. The Acapulco airport also experienced flooding, though service was not interrupted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aplane_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-aplane-71">[70]</a></sup> Throughout Mexico, the hurricane caused four deaths and $2.2\xc2\xa0billion (2006\xc2\xa0MXN, $203\xc2\xa0million 2006\xc2\xa0USD) in damage,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinal_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-sinal-72">[71]</a></sup> half of which in <a href="/wiki/Sinaloa" title="Sinaloa">Sinaloa</a> where heavy crop damage was reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinaloadamagetotal_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-sinaloadamagetotal-73">[72]</a></sup> An estimated 4,320\xc2\xa0homes were affected by the hurricane, and 19,200\xc2\xa0miles (30,000\xc2\xa0km) of roads and highways were damaged to some degree, including some destroyed bridges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinal_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-sinal-72">[71]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Miriam">Tropical Storm Miriam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Miriam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miriam06.jpg"><img alt="Miriam06.jpg" data-file-height="548" data-file-width="568" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Miriam06.jpg/150px-Miriam06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Miriam06.jpg/225px-Miriam06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Miriam06.jpg/300px-Miriam06.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miriam_2006_track.png"><img alt="Miriam 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Miriam_2006_track.png/150px-Miriam_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Miriam_2006_track.png/225px-Miriam_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Miriam_2006_track.png/300px-Miriam_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 16\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 September 18</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>45\xc2\xa0mph (75\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 999\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>A disturbance associated with a northerly extension of the <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">Intertropical Convergence Zone</a> and a tropical wave developed a closed circulation on September\xc2\xa015. It moved northeastward due to the influence from nearby Hurricane Lane, and organized enough to be declared Tropical Depression Fourteen-E on September\xc2\xa016 while located about 500\xc2\xa0miles southwest of <a href="/wiki/Cabo_San_Lucas" title="Cabo San Lucas">Cabo San Lucas</a>, Mexico. It quickly strengthened, and organized into Tropical Storm Miriam later that day. After reaching a peak intensity of 45\xc2\xa0mph (70\xc2\xa0km/h), vertical wind shear and cooler waters rapidly weakened the storm, and the circulation decoupled from the convection on September\xc2\xa017. After turning more towards the north, Miriam weakened to tropical depression status, and on September\xc2\xa018 it degenerated to a remnant low. The remnant circulation turned to the northwest, then to the east, and dissipated on September\xc2\xa021 a short distance west of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a>. No deaths are damage are associated with Miriam, and only one ship recorded winds of over tropical storm force near the center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miriamtcr_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-miriamtcr-74">[73]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Two-C">Tropical Depression Two-C</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Two-C">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:02C_TERRA_MODIS_30_kt_2006.jpg"><img alt="02C TERRA MODIS 30 kt 2006.jpg" data-file-height="3936" data-file-width="4096" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/02C_TERRA_MODIS_30_kt_2006.jpg/150px-02C_TERRA_MODIS_30_kt_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/02C_TERRA_MODIS_30_kt_2006.jpg/225px-02C_TERRA_MODIS_30_kt_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/02C_TERRA_MODIS_30_kt_2006.jpg/300px-02C_TERRA_MODIS_30_kt_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2-C_2006_track.png"><img alt="2-C 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/2-C_2006_track.png/150px-2-C_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/2-C_2006_track.png/225px-2-C_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/2-C_2006_track.png/300px-2-C_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 19\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 September 20</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>35\xc2\xa0mph (55\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1007\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On September\xc2\xa019, an area of disturbed weather associated with the <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">Intertropical Convergence Zone</a> became sufficiently organized to be designated Tropical Depression Two-C. Initially, it was thought that the depression formed from the remnants of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Kristy_(2006)" title="Hurricane Kristy (2006)">Hurricane Kristy</a>, although subsequent analysis confirmed they were two separate systems. Initially, the depression was in an area of favorable conditions, with little wind shear and warm waters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-5"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup> As a result, the CPHC predicted significant strengthening to at least hurricane status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> Instead, a high pressure system to its north increased wind shear over the depression, causing the convection to become removed from the center. The depression weakened into a remnant low on September\xc2\xa020, never reaching tropical storm status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-6"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Three-C">Tropical Depression Three-C</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Three-C">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TD_03C_2006_NRL.jpg"><img alt="TD 03C 2006 NRL.jpg" data-file-height="3600" data-file-width="3600" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/TD_03C_2006_NRL.jpg/150px-TD_03C_2006_NRL.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/TD_03C_2006_NRL.jpg/225px-TD_03C_2006_NRL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/TD_03C_2006_NRL.jpg/300px-TD_03C_2006_NRL.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:3-C_2006_track.png"><img alt="3-C 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/3-C_2006_track.png/150px-3-C_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/3-C_2006_track.png/225px-3-C_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/3-C_2006_track.png/300px-3-C_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 26\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 September 27</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>35\xc2\xa0mph (55\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1005\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>During September, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o-Southern_Oscillation" title="El Ni\xc3\xb1o-Southern Oscillation">El Ni\xc3\xb1o</a> conditions became established across the Pacific, which produced an area of warmer waters along the International Date Line. A few days after Tropical Depression Two-C dissipated, another area of disturbed weather formed, and although it was disorganized, it was also persistent. The CPHC initiated advisories on Tropical Depression Three-C on September\xc2\xa026 after a circulation was evident in the system. Strong wind shear prevented any development, and the system dissipated on September\xc2\xa027.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-7"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Norman">Tropical Storm Norman</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Norman">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_Norman_09_oct_2006_1849Z.jpg"><img alt="TS Norman 09 oct 2006 1849Z.jpg" data-file-height="3972" data-file-width="3972" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/TS_Norman_09_oct_2006_1849Z.jpg/150px-TS_Norman_09_oct_2006_1849Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/TS_Norman_09_oct_2006_1849Z.jpg/225px-TS_Norman_09_oct_2006_1849Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/TS_Norman_09_oct_2006_1849Z.jpg/300px-TS_Norman_09_oct_2006_1849Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Norman_2006_track.png"><img alt="Norman 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Norman_2006_track.png/150px-Norman_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Norman_2006_track.png/225px-Norman_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Norman_2006_track.png/300px-Norman_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>October 9\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 October 15</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>50\xc2\xa0mph (85\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1000\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Norman_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Norman (2006)">Tropical Storm Norman (2006)</a></div>\n<p>Early in October, a low pressure system began to organize to the west of the Mexican coast, and on October\xc2\xa09 it developed into Tropical Depression Fifteen-E. It strengthened into a tropical storm the next day, but strong wind shear and low sea-surface temperatures hindered development. Norman slowly began to weaken, and on October\xc2\xa011 it degenerated into a remnant low pressure area. Turning eastward, the system combined with a new tropical disturbance off the southwest Mexican coast, and slowly began to reorganize. The system was re-designated a tropical depression on October\xc2\xa015 just south-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Manzanillo,_Colima" title="Manzanillo, Colima">Manzanillo, Colima</a>, although within a few hours it again dissipated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norman_TCR_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Norman_TCR-76">[75]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The storm brought heavy rainfall to southwestern Mexico, peaking at 6.35\xc2\xa0inches (161\xc2\xa0mm) in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_Villita,_Michoac%C3%A1n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="La Villita, Michoac\xc3\xa1n (page does not exist)">La Villita, Michoac\xc3\xa1n</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> The rainfall caused flooding and mudslides around Acapulco, affecting 170\xc2\xa0homes, of which 20 were destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elun_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-elun-78">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lajo_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-lajo-79">[78]</a></sup> About 300\xc2\xa0hectares (740\xc2\xa0acres) of crop fields sustained damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lajo_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-lajo-79">[78]</a></sup> Initially there were two people missing;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lajo_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-lajo-79">[78]</a></sup> however, a subsequent report indicated there were no casualties associated with the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norman_TCR_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-Norman_TCR-76">[75]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Olivia">Tropical Storm Olivia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Olivia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_Olivia_09_oct_2006_2155Z.jpg"><img alt="TS Olivia 09 oct 2006 2155Z.jpg" data-file-height="3972" data-file-width="3972" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/TS_Olivia_09_oct_2006_2155Z.jpg/150px-TS_Olivia_09_oct_2006_2155Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/TS_Olivia_09_oct_2006_2155Z.jpg/225px-TS_Olivia_09_oct_2006_2155Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/TS_Olivia_09_oct_2006_2155Z.jpg/300px-TS_Olivia_09_oct_2006_2155Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Olivia_2006_track.png"><img alt="Olivia 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Olivia_2006_track.png/150px-Olivia_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Olivia_2006_track.png/225px-Olivia_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Olivia_2006_track.png/300px-Olivia_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>October 9\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 October 12</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>45\xc2\xa0mph (75\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1000\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On September\xc2\xa018, a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> exited <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and later crossed into the eastern <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> on September\xc2\xa029 without development. Convection increased in the Pacific along the wave axis, spawning a broad <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">low pressure area</a> on October\xc2\xa05. Despite the presence of <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, it organized enough for the NHC to initiate advisories on Tropical Depression Sixteen-E on October\xc2\xa09 about 1,360 miles (2,190\xc2\xa0km) to the west-southwest of the southern tip of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-otcr_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-otcr-80">[79]</a></sup> Influenced by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_pressure_system" title="High pressure system">high pressure system</a>, the depression drifted northward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> Six hours after being upgraded to a tropical storm, Olivia attained peak winds of 45\xc2\xa0mph (75\xc2\xa0km/h),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-otcr_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-otcr-80">[79]</a></sup> although the convection was limited to its northern side due to wind shear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> On October 11, the convective activity diminished and Olivia weakened to tropical depression status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> Olivia deteriorated into a remnant low on October\xc2\xa013. It moved towards the east-southeast, and on October\xc2\xa015 was absorbed into the remnants of <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Norman_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Norman (2006)">Tropical Storm Norman</a>. Olivia never affected land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-otcr_80-2"><a href="#cite_note-otcr-80">[79]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Four-C">Tropical Depression Four-C</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Four-C">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TD_4C_13_oct_2006_2143Z.jpg"><img alt="TD 4C 13 oct 2006 2143Z.jpg" data-file-height="3712" data-file-width="3712" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/TD_4C_13_oct_2006_2143Z.jpg/150px-TD_4C_13_oct_2006_2143Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/TD_4C_13_oct_2006_2143Z.jpg/225px-TD_4C_13_oct_2006_2143Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/TD_4C_13_oct_2006_2143Z.jpg/300px-TD_4C_13_oct_2006_2143Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:4-C_2006_track.png"><img alt="4-C 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/4-C_2006_track.png/150px-4-C_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/4-C_2006_track.png/225px-4-C_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/4-C_2006_track.png/300px-4-C_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>October\xc2\xa013\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 October\xc2\xa014</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>35\xc2\xa0mph (55\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1007\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>In the middle of October, the Intertropical Convergence Zone extended across the central Pacific Ocean, resembling an extension of the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon_trough" title="Monsoon trough">monsoon trough</a>. An area of disturbed weather formed well to the southwest of Hawaii, organizing slowly for several days. Late on October\xc2\xa013, after the development of a low-level circulation and persistent convection, the CPHC classified the system as Tropical Depression Four-C about 750\xc2\xa0mi (1,200\xc2\xa0km) southwest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honolulu,_Hawaii" title="Honolulu, Hawaii">Honolulu, Hawaii</a>. Upon being classified, the depression was located in an unusual <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone#Steering_winds" title="Tropical cyclone">steering flow</a> that caused it to track eastward. Due to the approach of an upper-level <a href="/wiki/Trough_(meteorology)" title="Trough (meteorology)">trough</a>, it was expected to dissipate quickly from <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, although forecasters noted the possibility for the trough to provide an <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a> channel, which might allow strengthening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> On October\xc2\xa014, strong wind shear removed the convection completely from the center, and the system degenerated into a remnant low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-8"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The remnant circulation continued slowly eastward, dissipating on October\xc2\xa016. Concurrently, the convection tracked northeastward ahead of the upper-level trough, which contributed to heavy rainfall and flooding on the island of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_(island)" title="Hawaii (island)">Hawaii</a> on October\xc2\xa017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-9"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup> The rainfall event coincided with an <a href="/wiki/2006_Kiholo_Bay_earthquake" title="2006 Kiholo Bay earthquake">Kiholo Bay earthquake</a> striking the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Paul">Hurricane Paul</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Hurricane Paul">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2\xc2\xa0hurricane\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Paul_23_oct_2006_2030Z.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane Paul 23 oct 2006 2030Z.jpg" data-file-height="5400" data-file-width="5400" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Hurricane_Paul_23_oct_2006_2030Z.jpg/150px-Hurricane_Paul_23_oct_2006_2030Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Hurricane_Paul_23_oct_2006_2030Z.jpg/225px-Hurricane_Paul_23_oct_2006_2030Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Hurricane_Paul_23_oct_2006_2030Z.jpg/300px-Hurricane_Paul_23_oct_2006_2030Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_2006_track.png"><img alt="Paul 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Paul_2006_track.png/150px-Paul_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Paul_2006_track.png/225px-Paul_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Paul_2006_track.png/300px-Paul_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>October 21\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 October 26</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>105\xc2\xa0mph (165\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 970\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Paul_(2006)" title="Hurricane Paul (2006)">Hurricane Paul (2006)</a></div>\n<p>Hurricane Paul developed from an area of disturbed weather on October\xc2\xa021, and slowly intensified as it moved into an area of warm waters and progressively decreasing wind shear. Paul attained hurricane status on October\xc2\xa023, and later that day it reached its peak intensity of 105\xc2\xa0mph (165\xc2\xa0km/h), a strong Category\xc2\xa02 hurricane on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson scale</a>. A strong trough turned the hurricane to the north and northeast into an area of strong vertical shear, and Paul weakened to a tropical storm on October\xc2\xa024, later passing just south of the Baja California Peninsula. Paul weakened to a tropical depression on October\xc2\xa025 a short distance off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, and after briefly turning away from the coast it made landfall on northwestern <a href="/wiki/Sinaloa" title="Sinaloa">Sinaloa</a> on October\xc2\xa026.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Paul was the third hurricane to threaten western Mexico in the season, the others being <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_John_(2006)" title="Hurricane John (2006)">Hurricanes John</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lane_(2006)" title="Hurricane Lane (2006)">Lane</a>. Rough surf killed two people along <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Sur" title="Baja California Sur">Baja California Sur</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canoe_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-canoe-87">[86]</a></sup> while two deaths from flooding were reported in <a href="/wiki/Sinaloa" title="Sinaloa">Sinaloa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> Paul dropped moderate rainfall across mainland Mexico, including a 24-hour total of 2.28\xc2\xa0inches (58\xc2\xa0mm) in <a href="/wiki/Mazatl%C3%A1n" title="Mazatl\xc3\xa1n">Mazatl\xc3\xa1n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sinaloa" title="Sinaloa">Sinaloa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomberg_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-89">[88]</a></sup> Damage totaled more than $35\xc2\xa0million (2006\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Mexican_peso" title="Mexican peso">MXN</a>, $3.2\xc2\xa0million 2006\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Eighteen-E">Tropical Depression Eighteen-E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Eighteen-E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TD_18E_26_oct_2006_1755Z.jpg"><img alt="TD 18E 26 oct 2006 1755Z.jpg" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="3000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/TD_18E_26_oct_2006_1755Z.jpg/150px-TD_18E_26_oct_2006_1755Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/TD_18E_26_oct_2006_1755Z.jpg/225px-TD_18E_26_oct_2006_1755Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/TD_18E_26_oct_2006_1755Z.jpg/300px-TD_18E_26_oct_2006_1755Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:18-E_2006_track.png"><img alt="18-E 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/18-E_2006_track.png/150px-18-E_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/18-E_2006_track.png/225px-18-E_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/18-E_2006_track.png/300px-18-E_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>October 26\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 October 27</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>35\xc2\xa0mph (55\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1007\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The origins of Tropical Depression Eighteen-E were from a tropical wave that exited the coast of Africa on October\xc2\xa07. It briefly spawned a low-pressure area as the wave continued westward without development. On October\xc2\xa020, the wave entered the Pacific Ocean, developing an area of thunderstorms about four days later. By 1200\xc2\xa0UTC on October\xc2\xa026, a tropical depression formed about 155\xc2\xa0mi (260\xc2\xa0km) south of Manzanillo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18Etcr_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-18Etcr-91">[90]</a></sup> Initially, Tropical Depression Eighteen-E was located in an area of light wind shear, and the NHC anticipated further organization and strengthening to near hurricane status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18disc1_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-18disc1-92">[91]</a></sup> The tropical depression initially maintained a steady westward motion away from the Mexican coastline, due to a ridge north of the cyclone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18disc1_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-18disc1-92">[91]</a></sup> By October\xc2\xa017, convection had decreased, and the depression was not forecast to intensify as much.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> Possibly due to intrusion of dry air, the circulation became exposed from the thunderstorms, and having weakened, it turned to a southward drift.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> By 0000\xc2\xa0UTC on October\xc2\xa028, the system had weakened to a non-convective remnant low, which dissipated the following day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18Etcr_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-18Etcr-91">[90]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Rosa">Tropical Storm Rosa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Rosa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_Rosa_09_nov_2006_1800Z.jpg"><img alt="TS Rosa 09 nov 2006 1800Z.jpg" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1200" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/TS_Rosa_09_nov_2006_1800Z.jpg/150px-TS_Rosa_09_nov_2006_1800Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/TS_Rosa_09_nov_2006_1800Z.jpg/225px-TS_Rosa_09_nov_2006_1800Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/TS_Rosa_09_nov_2006_1800Z.jpg/300px-TS_Rosa_09_nov_2006_1800Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rosa_2006_track.png"><img alt="Rosa 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Rosa_2006_track.png/150px-Rosa_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Rosa_2006_track.png/225px-Rosa_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Rosa_2006_track.png/300px-Rosa_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>November 8\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 November 10</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>40\xc2\xa0mph (65\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1002\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>A tropical wave exited western Africa on October\xc2\xa022 and continued westward into the Pacific on November\xc2\xa02, spawning a tropical depression on November\xc2\xa08 about 440\xc2\xa0mi (710\xc2\xa0km) south of <a href="/wiki/Manzanillo,_Colima" title="Manzanillo, Colima">Manzanillo, Colima</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rtcr_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-rtcr-95">[94]</a></sup> Environmental conditions appeared favorable,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> although wind shear removed the convection from the circulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> Throughout its duration, the storm maintained a northwest track through a weakness in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_pressure_system" title="High pressure system">subtropical ridge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc5_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc5-98">[97]</a></sup> By November\xc2\xa09, a new area of convection persisted near the center,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">banding feature</a> formed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc5_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-disc5-98">[97]</a></sup> Despite the shear, the depression was upgraded to Tropical Storm Rosa, although the shear prevented intensification beyond its peak of 40\xc2\xa0mph (65\xc2\xa0km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rtcr_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-rtcr-95">[94]</a></sup> Rosa remained a tropical storm for only 18\xc2\xa0hours, becoming a tropical depression early on November\xc2\xa010 and dissipating later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rtcr_95-2"><a href="#cite_note-rtcr-95">[94]</a></sup> Rosa was the first tropical storm in the basin to develop during November since 2000, and was also the first tropical depression to form in the month since 2002\'s <a href="/wiki/2002_Pacific_hurricane_season#Tropical_Depression_Sixteen-E" title="2002 Pacific hurricane season">Tropical Depression Sixteen-E</a>. No impact was reported from the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rtcr_95-3"><a href="#cite_note-rtcr-95">[94]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Twenty-E">Tropical Depression Twenty-E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Twenty-E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TD_20E_11_nov_2006_1755Z.jpg"><img alt="TD 20E 11 nov 2006 1755Z.jpg" data-file-height="3972" data-file-width="3972" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/TD_20E_11_nov_2006_1755Z.jpg/150px-TD_20E_11_nov_2006_1755Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/TD_20E_11_nov_2006_1755Z.jpg/225px-TD_20E_11_nov_2006_1755Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/TD_20E_11_nov_2006_1755Z.jpg/300px-TD_20E_11_nov_2006_1755Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20-E_2006_track.png"><img alt="20-E 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/20-E_2006_track.png/150px-20-E_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/20-E_2006_track.png/225px-20-E_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/20-E_2006_track.png/300px-20-E_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>November 11\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 November 11</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>35\xc2\xa0mph (55\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1007\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>A tropical wave moved off the western coast of Africa on October\xc2\xa021, briefly developing two weak low pressure areas before the wave crossed into the Pacific Ocean on November\xc2\xa01. Thunderstorm activity slowly increased as the wave interacted within the Intertropical Convergence Zone. After a curved band of convection developed, it is estimated the system formed into Tropical Depression Twenty-E around 0000\xc2\xa0UTC on November\xc2\xa011, about 550\xc2\xa0mi (1,050\xc2\xa0km) southwest of Manzanillo. Throughout its duration, the depression never completely separated from the Intertropical Convergence Zone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20etcr_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-20etcr-100">[99]</a></sup> When the NHC issued its first advisory on the depression, the agency predicted slight intensification to tropical storm status and for the depression to last at least two days. This was due to a forecast of gradually increasing wind shear after the first 24\xc2\xa0hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> Instead, the circulation became very elongated; it is estimated the cyclone degenerated into a trough by late on November\xc2\xa011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20etcr_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-20etcr-100">[99]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Sergio">Hurricane Sergio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Hurricane Sergio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2\xc2\xa0hurricane\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Sergio_15_nov_2006_1725Z.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane Sergio 15 nov 2006 1725Z.jpg" data-file-height="5112" data-file-width="5528" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Hurricane_Sergio_15_nov_2006_1725Z.jpg/150px-Hurricane_Sergio_15_nov_2006_1725Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Hurricane_Sergio_15_nov_2006_1725Z.jpg/225px-Hurricane_Sergio_15_nov_2006_1725Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Hurricane_Sergio_15_nov_2006_1725Z.jpg/300px-Hurricane_Sergio_15_nov_2006_1725Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sergio_2006_track.png"><img alt="Sergio 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Sergio_2006_track.png/150px-Sergio_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Sergio_2006_track.png/225px-Sergio_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Sergio_2006_track.png/300px-Sergio_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>November 13\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 November 20</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>110\xc2\xa0mph (175\xc2\xa0km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 965\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sergio_(2006)" title="Hurricane Sergio (2006)">Hurricane Sergio (2006)</a></div>\n<p>Just days after Tropical Depression Twenty-E degenerated into an open trough, Tropical Depression Twenty One-E developed from a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> on November\xc2\xa013 about 460\xc2\xa0miles (740\xc2\xa0km) south of <a href="/wiki/Manzanillo,_Colima" title="Manzanillo, Colima">Manzanillo, Colima</a>. It steadily intensified as it tracked southeastward, reaching peak winds of 110\xc2\xa0mph (175\xc2\xa0km/h) on November\xc2\xa015. Subsequently, it began to weaken due to increased <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> as it turned to the north. Sergio later turned to the west, remaining well off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, and it dissipated on November\xc2\xa020 about 320\xc2\xa0miles (515\xc2\xa0km) west-northwest of where it originally formed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stcr_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-stcr-102">[101]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Sergio produced light rainfall along the coast of Mexico, though its effects were minimal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sergiosmn_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-sergiosmn-103">[102]</a></sup> The formation of Sergio marked the 2006 season as the most active in 12\xc2\xa0years and the second season in which more than one tropical storm formed in November, after <a href="/wiki/1961_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1961 Pacific hurricane season">1961</a>. Sergio set records for the month of November in the basin. At the time, it was considered the strongest hurricane to form in the month; although it has since dropped to third after <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandra_(2015)" title="Hurricane Sandra (2015)">Sandra from 2015</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2011_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Kenneth" title="2011 Pacific hurricane season">Kenneth from 2011</a>. It is however, still considered the longest-lived November <a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">Pacific tropical cyclone</a> with a duration of seven days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epachurdat_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-epachurdat-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stcr_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-stcr-102">[101]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_systems">Other systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Other systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Storm_91C_01_nov_2006_2030Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5600" data-file-width="6000" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Storm_91C_01_nov_2006_2030Z.jpg/240px-Storm_91C_01_nov_2006_2030Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Storm_91C_01_nov_2006_2030Z.jpg/360px-Storm_91C_01_nov_2006_2030Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Storm_91C_01_nov_2006_2030Z.jpg/480px-Storm_91C_01_nov_2006_2030Z.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Storm_91C_01_nov_2006_2030Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe cyclone at peak intensity in the northeast Pacific, on November 1.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_Central_Pacific_cyclone" title="2006 Central Pacific cyclone">2006 Central Pacific cyclone</a></div>\n<p>On October 28, 2006, a cut-off extratropical cyclone stalled over the northeast Pacific Ocean and began to strengthen. By October 31, the storm had acquired tropical characteristics, including an <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a>, convection, and a warmer-than-average core. The system reached peak intensity on November 1, before slowly weakening and looping towards the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">Pacific Northwest</a>. The system made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington State</a> on November 3, before rapidly weakening and dissipating on the next day. During the duration of the storm, the system was known as Storm 91C (or INVEST 91C). The storm\'s true nature still remains controversial among meteorologists today, due to disputes over the storm\'s exact structure and whether or not it had obtained tropical or subtropical characteristics. Because the storm was not within the area of responsibility of the National Hurricane Center or the Central Pacific Hurricane Center, the storm was never assigned a name.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storm_names">Storm names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Storm names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The following names were used for named storms that formed in the northeast Pacific in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-name_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-name-104">[103]</a></sup> This is the same list that was used in the <a href="/wiki/2000_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2000 Pacific hurricane season">2000 season</a>. There were no names retired from the northeast Pacific list. Therefore, the same list was reused in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2012 Pacific hurricane season">2012 season</a>.</p>\n<table style="width:90%;">\n<tr>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Aletta_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Aletta (2006)">Aletta</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bud_(2006)" title="Hurricane Bud (2006)">Bud</a></li>\n<li>Carlotta</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Daniel_(2006)" title="Hurricane Daniel (2006)">Daniel</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Emilia_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Emilia (2006)">Emilia</a></li>\n<li>Fabio</li>\n<li>Gilma</li>\n<li>Hector</li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ileana_(2006)" title="Hurricane Ileana (2006)">Ileana</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_John_(2006)" title="Hurricane John (2006)">John</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Kristy_(2006)" title="Hurricane Kristy (2006)">Kristy</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lane_(2006)" title="Hurricane Lane (2006)">Lane</a></li>\n<li>Miriam</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Norman_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Norman (2006)">Norman</a></li>\n<li>Olivia</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Paul_(2006)" title="Hurricane Paul (2006)">Paul</a></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li>Rosa</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sergio_(2006)" title="Hurricane Sergio (2006)">Sergio</a></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Tara\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Vicente\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Willa\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Xavier\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Yolanda\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Zeke\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>For storms that form in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">Central Pacific Hurricane Center</a>\'s area of responsibility, encompassing the area between <a href="/wiki/140th_meridian_west" title="140th meridian west">140 degrees west</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a>, all names are used in a series of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tropical_cyclone_names#Central_Pacific" title="List of tropical cyclone names">four rotating lists</a>. The next four names that were slated for use in 2006 are shown below, however only the name <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ioke" title="Hurricane Ioke">Ioke</a> was used.</p>\n<table style="width:90%;">\n<tr>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ioke" title="Hurricane Ioke">Ioke</a></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Kika\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Lana\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Maka\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The name <i>Ioke</i> was <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_hurricane_names" title="List of retired Pacific hurricane names">retired</a> from the north-central Pacific list by the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> in the spring of 2007 and replaced with <i>Iopa</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> During the 61st Interdepartmental Hurricane Conference, the Hawaii State Civil Defense requested the retirement of the name <i>Daniel</i>, citing that the storm had become memorable due to threat of damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> However, the request was denied, as the name remains on the tropical cyclone naming list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-name_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-name-104">[103]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_effects">Season effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Season effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>This is a table of all the storms that have formed in the 2006 Pacific hurricane season. It includes their duration, names, landfall(s), denoted in parentheses, damages, and death totals. Deaths in parentheses are additional and indirect (an example of an indirect death would be a traffic accident), but were still related to that storm. Damage and deaths include totals while the storm was extratropical, a wave, or a low, and all the damage figures are in 2006 USD.</p>\n<table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="refbegin" style="">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Rainfall totals are rounded to the nearest 1/100th of an <a href="/wiki/Inch" title="Inch">inch</a> and to the nearest <a href="/wiki/Millimetre" title="Millimetre">millimetre</a>.</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-107"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-107">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Though <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ioke" title="Hurricane Ioke">Hurricane Ioke</a> did not make landfall, its strike on Wake Island is included in the table, due to the severe damage on the island.</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-108"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-108">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In its report on <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Norman_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Norman (2006)">Tropical Storm Norman</a>, the National Hurricane Center did not specify whether the storm moved ashore or not.
